According to the Teaching of St. Dionysius, they are distinguished into nine Choirs, which are again distributed into three Orders (τάξεις; see The Celestial Hierarchy, Chapters 6-9).[103]

The first Order is of those who are nearest to God, as the Seraphim, Cherubim, and Thrones.

In the second the Dominions, Powers, and Authorities.

In the third the Principalities, Archangels, Angels, and those all disposed in such Order, that all the lower Ranks are enlightened, and receive the divine blessings from the higher.

These Angels always continue in the love of God, having received this grace that they should be incapable of falling, because they listened not unto Lucifer, when he tempted them to rebel against God, through whose grace only it is that they are thus established, and not through their own strength.

And thus far we think it sufficient to treat in the small compass of this Confession, concerning the knowledge of Angels: Wherefore, since it is well enough known that the Angels do help us with their guardianship, and also assist us with their intercession, let us therefore, as we ought, entreat them, that they may pray to God for us. More especially the Angel who is appointed our guardian and guide.

21. What are we to think concerning evil Angels?

They are all created good by God; for whatsoever God made, it was good; but, through their own will, they became evil, as our Lord testifies of the Chief of the Devils:

He was a murderer from the beginning, and abode not in the truth, because there is no truth in him. When he speaks a lie, he speaks of his own; for he is a liar, and the Father of it. (John 8:44).

These are the authors and chiefs of all impiety, and continual blasphemers of the Divine Majesty. These are the deceivers of mankind, both they and their Instruments, according to the Scripture, Be sober, be vigilant, because your Adversary, the Devil, as a roaring lion walks about, seeking whom he may devour (1 Peter 5:8).

Nevertheless, be it known that the Devil cannot exercise any power, or offer any violence unto any man, or any thing, unless they are so permitted of God, as the Scripture witnesseth, The devils besought him, saying, “If you cast us out, suffer us to go away into the herd of swine”; and he said unto them, “Go” (Matthew 8:31-32). And let everyone be assured, that it is least of all in their power to compel man to sin; they can only tempt, and persuade us, by their instigation and deceit, to do evil and go astray: For man is endowed with a free will, which God himself will not constrain, nor lay under any necessity.

But forasmuch as the Devils are condemned unto everlasting punishment and torments, they can never become partakers of the divine mercy or grace; as it is said, Depart from me, you cursed, unto everlasting fire, prepared for the Devil and his Angels (Matthew 25:41).

22. What are we to believe concerning other created things?

As follows: That God, by his word and command, has made all things out of nothing (ex nihilo); and, lastly, created man, and appointed him the heir and lord of all things under heaven, saying:

Let us make man in our image, and after our likeness; and let them have dominion over the fish of the sea, and over the fowl of the air, and over the cattle, and over all the earth. (Genesis 1:26)

And the sacred Poet:

You make him to have dominion of the works of your hands; and you have put all things in subjection under his feet; all sheep and oxen, yea, and the beasts of the field, the fowls of the air, and the fishes of the sea, and whatsoever walks through the paths of the seas. (Psalm 8:6-8)

And a little before, You made him a little lower than the Angels, you have crowned him with glory and honor (Psalm 8:5).

But because he disobeyed the command of God in paradise, and took and ate of the forbidden fruit, therefore being at once deprived of all the honors and favors with which he had been adorned, whilst he held his integrity, he was driven out of the mansion, and became such as the Prophet David has described him, man that is in honor, and understands not, is like the beasts that perish, and is become like unto them (Psalm 49:20). And to the same purpose, Dust you are, and unto dust shall you return (Genesis 3:19).

On the Creation and Fall of Man.[104]

23. What was the state of innocence of man, or purity and freedom from sin?

The state of innocence and integrity was twofold, according to St. Basil (Homily 12: On the Beginning of Proverbs).

The first is a voluntary departure from sin: as when a man, of his own deliberate purpose, forsakes what he knows to be sin.

The other is simply not knowing sin: as when a person, either by reason of tender age, or any other cause, is without knowing or committing evil.

Of this last kind was the innocence of Adam before the Fall, joined with a most complete and perfect rectitude, and innate justice both of will and understanding. So that in his understanding all knowledge was included; and, in his will, all virtue and honesty.

For inasmuch as Adam had a perfect knowledge of God, therefore in knowing of God, he knew all other things through God, as appeared in that, when all the creatures came to Adam to be named: For he gave them all names expressive of the several natures and dispositions, which he knew not from any experience, but from that knowledge of things which, by the blessing of God, he had.

And as for his will, it was in all things governed by his reason; yet so as to retain a perfect freedom; and that it is manifestly in the power of man to sin, or not to sin, is evident from holy Scripture:

Say not: “It is through the Lord that I fell away.” For you ought not do the things which he hates. Say not: “He has caused me to err.” For he has no need of the sinful man. The Lord hates all abomination; and they that fear God love it not. He himself made man from the beginning, and left him in the hand of his counsel. If you will, you shall keep the commandments and faith by doing what pleases him. He has set fire and water before you; stretch forth your hand unto whither you will. Before man is life and death, and whichsoever he likes, it shall be given him. (Sirach 15:11-17)

And a little after, He has commanded no man to do wickedly; neither has he given any man licence to sin (Sirach 15:20).

In such a state of innocence and impeccability, like the Angels, was man: But when, by transgressing the commandments, he had sinned, he then came into a state of sin; and, being expelled from paradise, he became subject to death, according to that Scripture, The wages of sin is death (Romans 6:28); and presently losing the perfection of his reason and understanding, his will deviates (ἐκκλίνω) to evil rather than good.

Thus the state of innocence and integrity, by man tasting of evil, became a state of sin (κατάστασιν ἁμαρτίας); and man, who before was perfect, debased so low that now he may well cry out with David, I am a worm, and no man (Psalm 22:6).

24. Whether all men are liable for the sin of Adam?

As all mankind, during the state of innocence, was in Adam; so in him all men, falling from what he fell, remained in a state of sin (κατάστασιν ἁμαρτίας).

Wherefore mankind is become, not only subject unto sin, but also, on account of sin, unto punishment; which, according to the sentence pronounced of God, was, In the day that you eat of the Tree, you shall surely die (Genesis 2:17). And to this the Apostle alludes, Wherefore as by one man sin entered into the world, and death by sin, and so death passed upon all men, for all have sinned (Romans 5:12).

So that we are conceived in our mother’s womb, and born in this sin, according to the holy Psalmist, Behold, I was shaped in wickedness, and in sin has my mother conceived me (Psalm 51:5).

This is called Ancestral Sin (from the Greek: προπατορικό, propatoriko; Latin: Avitum):[105]

First, because that, before this, mankind was free from all sin; although the Devil was then corrupt, and fallen, by whose temptation this Ancestral Sin sprang (εβλάστησε) up in man; and Adam becoming subjected (υποκείμενος), we all likewise, who descend from him, also fall (καταβαίνομεν).

Secondly, because mankind is seized (συλλαμβάνεται) in sin.[106]

25. But since God foreknew that Adam would fall, wherefore, I pray, did he create him liable to it?

God fully foreknew both the Fall of Adam, and the malice of Lucifer, before he created either, and the most minute thoughts and actions that either of them would think or act; nevertheless the divine Goodness would not suffer itself to be overcome by the wickedness of man, or the Devil, but, that it might be the more manifest, God created the Devil a good Angel, who, of his own free will and choice, became evil: as afterwards man did by his temptation (cf. St. John of Damascus, On the Orthodox Faith, Book 2, Chapter 27; also his Dialogue Against the Manichees).[107]

Now, God so dealt with mankind, that, in his disobedience, God's goodness might shine with more glorious brightness, by sending his only Son into this world, who might take flesh of a most unspotted Virgin, by the operation (συνεργίαν) of the Holy Spirit and redeem lost man; and receive him into his Kingdom, adorned with greater glory than he had before in paradise, to the eternal confusion of the Devil. Therefore neither ought the sin of man hinder, that God should not create him.

26. Since, then, God knew all things before they were, did he not predestine them to be good or evil, in such a way that they could not be otherwise than they are?

God certainly foreknew all things before they were in being; but he only predestined good, for it were contrary to the divine Goodness to predestine evil (St. John of Damascus, On the Orthodox Faith, Book 2, Chapter 30).

For evil is no other than sin; for, except sin, which is the transgressing of the divine will and Law, properly speaking, there is no such thing as evil in the world: For those which God is pleased to inflict on us for our sins, as pestilence, war, sickness, and such like, they are said to be evil with regard to us, because they afflict us with pain and sorrow, to which we are averse: But, with regard, to God, they are not evil, but rather good, as being the instruments of his correction, whereby he converts us to righteousness (St. Basil the Great, Homily Explaining that God Is Not the Cause of Evil). Therefore when the Scripture says, Shall there be evil in a city, and the Lord has not done it? (Amos 3:6) there by the word evil is to be understood the just judgment of God.

In fine, God, in his wisdom and justice, predetermines only those things which are entirely out of our power, with regard to their being or not being; and in those good things which are in our power to be done, he foreknows, but so that his will hinders not ours, which no way controls the nature of free-will.

27. What is free-will?

Man’s free-will is an absolute, free, and voluntary choice to do good or evil, arising from reason or the rational soul.

For it is necessary that a being endued with reason, should have a nature joined with a power over his own will, which, as reason prompted, he should exercise freely.

Now reason, whilst man remained in the State of Innocence (that is, before his Fall) was perfect and uncorrupt; and by his Fall, became corrupt; but his will (although with regard to the desire of good and evil, it remained unaltered), yet, in some things, it became more inclined to the evil, and in others to the good: As says St. Basil the Great, Every man may by his will and choice become either a good seed or a bad (Commentary on Isaiah, Chapter 14); according to the Apostle, In Jesus Christ I have begotten you through the Gospel (1 Corinthians 4:15).

Also St. John, As many as received him, to them he gave power to become the sons of God (John 1:12). Wherein the holy teacher teaches us that notwithstanding the will of man is damaged (or harmed, from the Greek: ἐβλάβη; Latin: misere labefactata fuerit, or: weakened miserably) by Ancestral Sin (Greek: προπατορικόν ἁμάμαρτημα; Latin: peccato originis); yet it is the choice of every one whether he will become righteous, and the child of God; or wicked, and the child of the Devil. This, I say, is in every one’s power, but with the divine grace assisting (συμβοηθός) him to do good, and withdrawing him from evil; yet, nevertheless, so as not to interfere with his free will.

28. Seeing that man is born in sin, is the soul, as well as the body, from the seed of Adam?

The human body descends from Adam, but the soul comes from God: According to the Scripture, The Lord who stretches out the heavens, and lays the foundation of the earth, and forms the spirit of man within him (Zechariah 12:1). And again, Then shall the dust return to the earth as it was, and the spirit shall return to God who gave it (Ecclesiastes 12:7). For if the soul were of human seed, doubtless it would die with the body, and, with that, return to dust; but we are taught otherwise in the holy Scriptures, where Christ says to the thief on the cross, Verily I say unto you, This day you will be with me in Paradise (Luke 23:43). The body of the thief remained on the cross, but the soul, as being an immortal spirit, entered with Christ into Paradise: Whereas, if it had been of human extract, it must have died with the body on the cross. And, indeed, how can we otherwise understand these words of our Lord?

Have you not read that which was spoken to you by God, saying, “I am, the God of Abraham, and the God of Isaac, and the God of Jacob”? God is not the God of the dead, but of the living. (Matthew 22:31)

Which words cannot be applied but to the soul, for the bodies of those Fathers had been long ago consumed to dust; they must, therefore, be meant of the soul, which, as it lives forever, so it forever stands in the presence of God. Now, if the soul were of the same stock with the body, without doubt it must run the same fate with it, and together with it also perish. But the soul is immitted into the body by God, when he has fitted and prepared it for its reception, and is diffused throughout all its parts, as fire pervades all parts of the glowing iron. But chiefly it resides in the head and heart.

29. Since God is the Creator of all things, should he not also provide for all things?

He does provide entirely for all things: For from the smallest to the greatest, he knows them all, and every individual which he has made he particularly takes care of. For so says our blessed Savior:

Are not two sparrows sold for a penny? and not one of them shall fall on the ground apart from your Father. But the very hairs of your head are all numbered. (Matthew 10:29-30)

The same Providence David celebrates in the Old Testament:

The eyes of all wait upon you, and you give them their food in due season. You open your hand, and satisfy the desire of every living thing. (Psalm 145:15-16)

30. Are the words Foreknowledge, Predestination, and Providence, of the same signification in Divinity?

Foreknowledge, Predestination, and Providence have different energy (ἐνεργείαις) in Divinity.

Providence respects things which are already created, but Foreknowledge and Predestination were in God before any thing was created, but in a manner distinct from each other; Foreknowledge being the bare, simple knowing of a future thing, without any determinate specification of it: that is, not necessarily determining that this or that should be.

But Predestination, joined with Foreknowledge, is a determining of the species, or what a thing must be absolutely; only, always determining good, and not evil.

For if Predestination were to appoint evil, it would be contrary to the essential goodness of God: Therefore, in like manner, as we first conceive a thing, and then appoint concerning it, so may we speak with regard to God: First in order is his Foreknowledge; then his Predestination; and lastly (things being brought into actual being) his Providence. As the Apostle plainly teaches:

For whom he foreknew, he also predestined... And whom he predestined, these he also called; and whom he called, these he also justified; and whom he justified, these he also glorified. (Romans 8:29-30)

But this is only to be understood of man, for other created beings (except the Angels, who are settled in a state of certainty and safety) are not the objects of the divine Predestination; For, as they have no free will, so they are without imputation whatever they do, being done by the impulse of natural instinct; wherefore they are neither chastised with punishment of any kind, nor crowned with the rewards of glory and praise.

31. What does this Article further teach, concerning God and his creation?

Whatever your mind can possibly imagine good, that consider as appertaining to God, the supreme Good, as its Origin and Source; and whatever you can figure to yourself of evil, consider as the most opposite and remote from God: Not so much as being distant in place, as being different in its very essence.

Of created things, think thus: That they are good, as being produced by an infinitely good Maker; only with this difference, that rational beings, who are endued with understanding and free will, are bad when they depart from God. Not that they were so created, but for that they became so by acting contrary to their reason.

Of irrational beings, that as they are without free will, they are in their nature good.

c2X7

The Second Article: Of Christology.

32. What is the Second Article of the Faith?

And in one Lord Jesus Christ; the Son of God; the Only-begotten; Begotten of the Father before all ages; Light of Light; true God of true God; begotten, not made; of one essence with the Father; by whom all things were made.

33. What does this Article of the Creed teach us?

Chiefly two things.

First, That the Son of God, Jesus Christ, is God eternal, of the same proper nature with his Father, and equal to him in glory and honor: as he says of himself, And now, Father, glorify me together with yourself, with the glory which I had with you before the world was (John 17:5).

Secondly, That Jesus Christ is the Creator, not only of the things which are made, but also of time itself, in which all things are made, by whom also he has made the Ages (Hebrews 1:2). But concerning permanent beings, the Evangelist says, The world was made by him, and the world knew him not (John 1:10).

34. What do the words Jesus Christ mean, which we meet with in this Article?

Jesus signifies Savior, as it is interpreted by the Archangel, who said unto Joseph, She shall bring forth a Son, and you shall call his Name Jesus, for he shall save his people from their sins (Matthew 1:21). Wherefore this Name cannot properly be given unto anyone, save only unto our Lord and Savior, who has set free all mankind from the bondage of the Devil.

Christ signifies Anointed: for that, in the Old Law, those who were anointed were called Christs: namely, Priests, Kings, and Prophets, into which three Offices Christ was anointed; not after the common manner of others, but after a superior manner, above all others: As the holy Psalmist says:

You have loved righteousness and hated iniquity; wherefore God, even your God, has anointed you with the oil of gladness, above your fellows (Psalm 45:7).

Wherein is meant, being anointed with the Holy Spirit, he was anointed according to the Prophet Isaiah: The Spirit of the Lord is upon me, because the Lord has Anointed me, to preach good Tidings unto the Meek (Isaiah 61:1). Which words Christ applies to himself, Today is this Scripture fulfilled in your hearing (Luke 4:21). Christ, indeed, was, with a three-fold excellency, and extraordinary majesty, exalted above his fellows.

Christ in His Three Offices.

First, as Priest after the Order of Melchizedek, according to the Apostle, Called of God an High Priest, after the Order of Melchizedek (Hebrews 5:10). And again, he calls Christ a Priest, because he offered himself to God and the Father, saying, Who through the eternal Spirit, offered himself without spot to God (Hebrews 9:14; cf. 9:11). And again, So Christ was once offered to bear the sins of many (Hebrews 9:28).

Secondly, The next excellency and majesty of Christ, in his Kingly Office, as the Archangel Gabriel declared when he brought the heavenly Annunciation to the most pure Virgin, saying:

The Lord God shall give unto him the throne of his father David, and he shall reign over the House of Jacob forever, and of his kingdom there shall be no end. (Luke 1:32-33)

The Wise Men, also, when they brought their offerings, testified concerning his Kingdom, saying, Where is he that is born King of the Jews? (Matthew 2:2) And the title given him at his Death confirms this, when it was written, Jesus of Nazareth, the King of the Jews (John 19:19).

Thirdly, Concerning his third Office, as Prophet, Moses long before had prophesied, by inspiration, saying, I will raise them up a Prophet from among their brethren, like unto you (Deuteronomy 18:18). This greatness of our Lord appears sufficiently from the sanctity of the doctrine which he taught; from whence, also, his Divinity is sufficiently manifest, and in which we are taught everything necessary to salvation. As he himself said, I have made your Name known unto them (John 17:26). And a few verses earlier:

For I have given unto them the words which you gave me, and they have received them, and have known surely that I come out from you, and they have believed that you sent me. (John 17:8)

But Christ more especially exercised this third Office of Prophet when he foretold what would come to pass; which he did, not by inspiration as other Prophets, but as God himself, of his own knowledge, as being God and man.

35. Why is the Son of God called Only-begotten?

That the Son of God is Only-begotten is manifest from the Scripture, We have seen his glory, the glory as of the only-begotten of the Father (John 1:14). And again, The only-begotten Son which is in the bosom of the Father (John 1:18). He is called Only-begotten, because he only is the Son of God by nature: Others, who are sometimes called the sons of God, are so, not by nature but by grace, or adoption, as the faithful and elect. Which grace of adoption, to become the sons of God, is granted them through Jesus Christ, according to the Scripture, As many as received him, to them gave the power to become the sons of God (John 1:12).

36. What do the words Light of Light mean?

For the better understanding of this, you are to know that there are two kinds of light, namely, created and Uncreated. Of the created light Scripture says:

God said, “Let there be light,” and there was light; and God saw the light that it was good, and God divided the light from the darkness. (Genesis 1:3)

But touching on the Uncreated Light, the Prophet Isaiah says:

The sun shall no more be your light by day, neither for brightness shall the moon give light unto you; but the Lord shall be an everlasting Light, and your God your glory. Your Sun shall no more go down, neither shall your Moon withdraw itself; for the Lord shall be your everlasting Light. (Isaiah 60:19-20)

And it is this Uncreated Light which is intended in this place, as more plainly appears from the words which immediately follow, namely, true God of true God; begotten, not made.

Created Light you are to consider as being made out of nothing (ex nihilo); but the Begotten Light, or the Son, as springing from the essence of the Father (οὐσίαν τοῡ Πατρός). As says the Apostle:

Who, being the brightness of his glory, and the express image of his person, and upholding all things by the word of his power, when he had by himself purged our sins, sat down on the right hand of the majesty on high. (Hebrews 1:3)

After the same manner he speaks of himself, I am the Light of the world; he that follows me shall not walk in darkness, but shall have the Light of Life (John 8:12).

Furthermore, it is said Light of Light, because he has in himself the whole essence of the Father; as when one light is kindled by another, it has in it all the nature of that other light.

Lastly, the words, by whom all things were made, are thus to be understood: As the Son is equal (ὁμοίως) in the same essence (ὁμοούσιος) with God the Father, so he is equally (ὁμοίως) Creator; and not interpreting by whom as by a servant or instrument, but by nature (ὡς φησὶν), for as the Scripture teaches, He was in the world, and the world was made through(διά) him (John 1:10); that is, by(ἐκ) him.

c2YJ

The Third Article: Of the Incarnation.

37. What is the Third Article of the Creed?

Who for us men, and for our salvation, came down from heaven, and was incarnate of the Holy Spirit and the Virgin Mary, and became man.

38. What does this Article of the Creed teach?

We are hereby taught four things:

First, That the Son of God came down from heaven into the womb of the most pure Virgin Mary, to save mankind, as he before had promised. Wherefore he thus speaks concerning himself, No man has ascended up to heaven but he that came down from heaven, even the Son of Man (John 3:13).

Now, he did not come down from heaven by change of place; for, as being very God, he fills all places, and is present in all; but so it seemed good unto his majesty, to humble himself by taking upon himself the human nature.

Secondly, This Article teaches us that our Lord Jesus Christ did verily and indeed take upon himself a real humanity, and not in appearance only. For in that moment wherein the blessed Virgin answered the Angel, and said, Behold the handmaid of the Lord, be it unto me according to your word (Luke 1:38), his body was formed in the Virgin’s womb, and he became a perfect man in every particular, and having a rational soul conjoined with his divinity, being perfect God and perfect man, in one and the same Person (cf. St. John of Damascus, On the Orthodox Faith, Book 3, Chapter 2). And the most pure Virgin was saluted, and acknowledged to be the Theotokos, as Elizabeth said unto her, And whence is this to me, that the Mother of my Lord should come to me? (Luke 1:43)

Furthermore, it behoves us to know that the Divinity was not changed into the humanity, neither was the humanity lost in the Divinity, but each nature remained complete with all its properties, only joined in one Person (hypostasis; Greek: εἰς μίαν ὑπόστασιν; Latin: in persona una); sin only, which appertained to the human nature, being excepted.

On Mariology.

39. What is the third thing taught in this Article?

Thirdly, we are hereby taught that the Incarnation of Christ was by the co-operation of the Holy Spirit (συνεργίαν τοῡ ἁγίου Πνεύματος); so that as the blessed Virgin was a virgin before his conception, so also in conceiving, after she had conceived, and even when she brought forth, she remained a Virgin. For Christ came forth of his Mother’s womb in such a manner as to leave unviolated her virginity and left unbroken that seal, that she might remain a Virgin forever.

40. What is the fourth thing contained in this Article?

Fourthly, Concerning the most pure Virgin, the Theotokos (God-bearer), Mary, whom all the Orthodox - as it is their duty - ought to praise and reverence as the Mother of our Lord Jesus Christ, or rather as the Theotokos and Mother of God, seeing she was thought worthy, by God, to fulfill so great a mystery. For which reason the Church has composed a salutation to her, partly with the words of the Archangel and holy Elizabeth, and partly with a form of her own:

O Virgin Theotokos, rejoice, Mary, full of grace, the Lord is with thee. Blessed art thou among women, and blessed is the Fruit of thy womb, for thou hast borne the Savior of our souls!

41. What are we to think concerning this salutation?

First, You must believe that this salutation was originally appointed by God himself: though it was taught unto men by the Archangel Gabriel, who has not dared to have used it, unless he had been so commanded by God.

Secondly, The words of the holy Elizabeth were also inspired by the Holy Spirit, as is evident from the Evangelist's account:

Elizabeth was filled with the Holy Spirit, and she spoke out with a loud voice, and said, “Blessed art thou among women, and blessed is the Fruit of thy womb.” (Luke 1:41-42)

Also the words which the Church has added are of the Holy Spirit.

And the Church, by the authority with which she is vested, does command us, that when we pray, we should frequently honor and praise the blessed Virgin with this salutation.

42. What is taught us in this salutation?

In this salutation is contained a commemoration, that the Son of God became man, and of the benefits which we receive thereby: And also we learn thereby, that when the eternal Word of God, who is without beginning, came down from heaven he brought not flesh with him, but received it in the womb of the most holy Virgin, formed of her purest blood, by the co-operation of the Holy Spirit (τοῡ ἁγίου συνεργοῦντος); so that he was born of her as of his proper mother.

And this we must most truly and firmly believe; for the Church does condemn, as heretics, all such as hold that the Savior came down from heaven already clothed with flesh, as if he passed through the holy Virgin as through a channel. (St. John of Damascus, On the Orthodox Faith, Book 3, Chapter 12; cf. St. Cyril of Jerusalem, Twelfth Catechetical Lecture)

We are, furthermore, taught therein to call the blessed Virgin the Theotokos (God-bearer; Latin: Deipara), according to the human nature of Christ; and that Christ, who was born of her, was perfect God, and perfect man.

Moreover, this salutation, in calling the Virgin full of grace, teaches us, that as she is the Mother of God (μήτηρ Θεοῦ), she is made more abundantly a partaker of the divine grace than any created being: Wherefore the Church rightly extolls her above the Cherubim and the Seraphim. For she, far above all the choirs of Angels, is at the right hand of her Son, with all honor and glory, according to David, At your right hand stood the Queen... arrayed in a vesture of inwoven gold, adorned in varied colors (Psalm 45:9, 13-14).

Every orthodox Christian ought to repeat this salutation with the utmost reverence, and implore the intercession of the Virgin; for the prayer of the Mother avails much with the Son.

And whosoever would be a devout honorer of the Virgin, let him - always standing, not sitting - repeat the Akathist Hymn, and other supplicatory canons (Greek: paraklesis; Slavonic: molieben) and hymns, which the Church has composed in honor of the Mother of God.

c2ZP

The Fourth Article: Of the Passion of Christ.

43. What is the Fourth Article of Creed?[108]

And he was crucified for us under Pontius Pilate, suffered, and was buried.

44. What is taught in the Fourth Article of the Creed?

Chiefly six things.

First, That the Word verily, and indeed, suffered on the Cross for our sakes, and truly and really died, according to that same humanity which he received from the Virgin Mary: As is manifest from the holy Book:

And when Jesus had cried with a loud voice, he said, “Father, into your hands I commit my spirit”; and having said this he gave up the spirit. (Luke 23:46)

And that he truly poured out his precious Blood for us, wherewith he redeemed us, as the Apostle bears witness:

Who has predestined us unto the adoption of children, by Jesus Christ... in whom we have redemption through his blood, the forgiveness of sins according to the riches of his grace. (Ephesians 1:5, 7)

45. What is the second thing contained in this Article?

That Christ suffered the punishment of us sinners, having no sin in himself: as the Apostle St. Peter testifies:

Forasmuch as you know you were not redeemed with corruptible things, as silver and gold, from the futile ways taught you by your fathers, but with the precious blood of Christ, as of a lamb without blemish and without spot. (1 Peter 1:18-19)

In like manner does John the Baptist bear witness, that Jesus, who was perfectly innocent, and free from any stain of sin, suffered for our sins; For thus says he, Behold the Lamb of God who takes away the sin of the world (John 1:29).

And this was voluntarily, and of his own free will, as he himself says, I have power to lay down my life, and I have power to take it up again (John 10:18).

46. What is the third thing taught?

That Christ suffered on the Cross, according to his human nature, not according to his Divinity. For his divine nature suffered not, was not fastened to the Cross, did not give its face to be spit upon, nor to the smiters: the divine nature died not. And that Christ was crucified only in the flesh the apostle clearly teaches, saying:

Now has he reconciled in the body of his flesh through death, to present you holy, and blameless, and above reproach before him. (Colossians 1:22)

Nevertheless his divine nature, having taken to it the humanity, was never again separated from it. Not in the time of his passion and death upon the Cross; not even in death; although his soul was separated from his body, yet did not his divinity ever depart from his body or his soul. So that in death itself Christ still continued one and the same person (cf. St. John of Damascus, On the Orthodox Faith, Book 3, Chapter 27).

47. What is the fourth part contained in this Article?

That the death of Christ was superabundantly more excellent, and of far greater benefits, than could be the death of all other men: For these especial reasons.

First, Because of the heavy burden of our sins, as says the Prophet Isaiah:

He has borne our griefs and carried our sorrows, yet we did esteem him stricken, smitten of God, and afflicted. But he was wounded for our transgressions, he was bruised for our iniquities. (Isaiah 53:4-5)

Also the Prophet Jeremiah, speaking in the person of Christ:

Is it nothing to you, all you who pass by? Behold and see if there is any sorrow like my sorrow, which has been brought on me, which the Lord has inflicted in the day of His fierce anger. (Lamentations 1:12)

Secondly, For that on the Cross he fulfilled his priestly office, offering himself to God and the Father, for the redemption of mankind: as the Apostle speaks concerning him, Who gave himself a ransom for all (1 Timothy 2:6). And again, Christ loved us, and has given himself for us, an offering and a sacrifice to God, for a sweet-smelling aroma (Ephesians 5:2). Also in another place, While we were yet sinners, Christ died for us (Romans 5:8).

Thirdly, Because on the Cross he completed the reconciliation which he had undertaken between God and man; as the aforementioned Apostle declared:

By him to reconcile all things unto himself, having made peace through the blood of his Cross... Blotting out the handwriting of ordinances that was against us; which was contrary to us; and took it out of the way, nailing it to the Cross. (Colossians 1:20; 2:14)

48. What is the fifth thing contained in this Article?

Concerning the burial of our Lord Jesus Christ, as he was really and truly fastened to the Cross, and underwent the most grievous torments, so was he verily and indeed dead, and buried in an honorable place; which came to pass for this end, that from henceforth none should doubt of the real Resurrection of Christ from the dead.

For had he been buried in an obscure by-place, and, as we say, in a corner, it would have given good occasion to the Jews to have opposed our Lord with their slanders: Wherefore, that the glorious Resurrection of Christ might be more unquestionable and glorious, the Jews, as if they had been directed by providence, go to Pilate, and say unto him:

“Command therefore that the sepulchre be made sure until the third day”: and Pilate said unto them, “You have a watch; go your way, make it as sure as you can.” So they went and made the sepulchre sure, sealing the stone, and setting a watch. (Matthew 27:64-66)

This watch of the Jews afforded a most certain and manifest proof of Christ's Resurrection; being struck with great dread at the time it was come to pass, as the Scripture informs us:

And behold there was a great earthquake, for an Angel of the Lord descended from heaven, and came and rolled lack the stone from the door, and sat upon it... and for fear of him the guards did shake and became as dead men. (Matthew 28:2, 4)

Who afterwards, going into the City, told the chief Priests all that had happened (Matthew 28:11). The guards, being as it were constrained to testify what they had witnessed, reported what the women were told by the Angel:

I know that you seek Jesus that was crucified. He is not here, for he is risen, as he said; come and see the place where the Lord lay, and go quickly, and tell his disciples that he is risen from the Dead. (Matthew 28:5-7)

For this cause, therefore, it was that the sepulchre of our Lord should be in a place of honor, that it might be clear to all that his disciples did not steal him away and bury him in an unknown obscure place, as the perverse Jews gave out, having corrupted the guards with large amounts of money. But this empty suspicion was fully confuted by the tomb itself, wherein our Lord had been buried, and by the sealing of the stone, and by the guard which the Jews had set. Besides, Joseph and Nicodemus were men of great honor and account in their nation.

Lastly, The precious linen wherein the dead body of our Lord had been wrapped, and the napkin which was about his head, remained folded up in the sepulchre after he was arisen; all which sufficiently proved that his body had not been secretly conveyed away by the disciples, but was indeed returned to life.

To this it deserves to be added that according to the holy prophecies it was of necessity that our Lord's sepulchre should be honorable, as it is, and has been: for so says the Prophet Isaiah, And his resting place shall be glorious (Isaiah 11:10). Now, whosoever visits this sepulchre, in faith and love of Christ, he shall obtain pardon of many sins; coming through that, in his mind, unto Christ himself.

49. From what has been said, I now desire to know in what place the soul of Christ remained after its departure from his body, and before his Resurrection.

The soul of Christ, although separated from his body, yet remained joined to his divinity and together with it went down to Hades: although no mention is made thereof in this Article, yet we are sufficiently certified that it is so by many hymns of the Church on this subject, which teach that Christ, together with his soul and his divinity, descended into Hades. As this troparion, or hymn of the Church, particularly sets forth:

In the grave bodily,

but in Hades with thy soul as God;

In Paradise with the thief,

And on the throne with the Father and the Spirit

Wast thou who fillest all things,

O Christ the Inexpressible.[109]

And having delivered from thence the souls of the holy Fathers, he led them into Paradise, together with the thief who had believed on him when he was crucified.

On the Sign of the Cross.

50. What is the sixth thing contained in this Article?

This Article, by making mention of the Cross on which Christ died and wrought the great work of our salvation, prompts us to comment something concerning it: Of which the Apostle St. Paul thus speaks:

God forbid that I should glory, except in the Cross of our Lord Jesus Christ: whereby the world is crucified unto me, and I unto the world. (Galatians 6:14)

And again, The preaching of the Cross is to them that perish foolishness; but unto us which are saved it is the power of God (1 Corinthians 1:18).

For many and great reasons, therefore, the Cross is venerable unto us, as the peculiar sign of Christ, on which a wonderful power is bestowed of putting evil spirits to flight: Forasmuch as it was anointed with the blood of the Son of God, who breathed out his soul thereon. To this purpose hear St. Cyril, Bishop of Jerusalem:

When we sign ourselves with the venerable sign of the Cross, the Devil then being mindful that Christ was nailed to the Cross for our salvation, and for the destruction of his hellish power, can no longer be present nor withstand the power of the Cross; but he flees from us and ceases to tempt us, more especially as we usually call upon the Name of our savior Christ at the same time. (St. Cyril of Jerusalem, Catechetical Lecture 13.36)[110]

Wherefore it is necessary that we should frequently sign ourselves with this holy sign; forasmuch as we perceive ourselves too commonly beset with the temptations of the Devil, which we cannot otherwise drive away than by the sign of the life-giving Cross, and seriously calling upon the Name of Jesus Christ. And by this, we not only drive away the insults of the spirits of darkness from ourselves, but also from whatever belongs to us; from our meat and our drink, from our utensils, and everything appertaining to us. Wherefore St. Cyril, in the place before mentioned, says further:

Bless thyself with the venerable sign of the Cross, when you eat and when you drink; when you stand and when you sit; when you speak and when you walk. Begin not any business or employment without first making this reverend sign; in your house or on the way, in the day or in the night, and in all places. (St. Cyril of Jerusalem, Catechetical Lecture 13.36)

51. After what manner ought we to form the sign of the venerable and life-giving Cross?

After this manner: First, with your thumb and two fingers (held together, and the fourth and fifth fingers pressing down on the palm), touch your forehead, saying, In the Name of the Father; Then in the same manner touch your chest (Greek: θώρακα, thoraka), saying, and of the Son; then touch your right shoulder, saying, and of the Holy Spirit; And, lastly, complete the sign of the Cross, by touching your left shoulder, saying, Amen.[111]

You may, also, when you Cross yourself, say thus, Lord Jesus Christ, Son of God, have mercy on me, a sinner. Amen.[112]

The Fifth Article: Of the Resurrection of Christ.

52. What is the Fifth Article of the Faith?

Who arose the third day from the dead, according to the Scriptures.

53. What are we taught by this Article of the Faith?

Two things.

First, That our Lord, Jesus Christ, returned to life by the power of his divinity, that the Son of Man must be delivered into the hands of sinful men, and be crucified, and the third day rise again (Luke 24:27).

And, Secondly, That he arose in that same individual body wherewith he was born, and died (John 20:27).

54. According to what Scripture did it so become Christ to suffer and to die, and also to rise on the Third Day?

The holy Scriptures are twofold; of the Old and of the New Testament.

The former, namely the Old Testament, foretold that Christ should come, and also the manner in which he should redeem mankind; namely, by suffering, dying and arising again from the dead: Therefore, according to those Scriptures, all these things were to be fulfilled by Christ. (cf. Psalm 16:8-11; Psalm 2:7; Psalm 21:25-27 (LXX); Psalm 40:1-3; Psalm 49:15; Isaiah 53:10; Hosea 6:1-2; et al.)

And by the latter, namely, the New Testament, it is manifestly confirmed, that Christ did fulfill all these things, and that he came into the world for that very cause whereof it was before written, as he says of himself, The Son of Man indeed goes just as it is written of him (Mark 14:21). And again, after his Resurrection, to his two disciples as they were journeying, Ought not Christ to have suffered these things, and to enter into his glory? And beginning at Moses, and all the Prophets, he expounded unto them, in all the Scriptures, the things concerning himself (Luke 24:26-27).

Now, that the Old Testament ought to have full and satisfactory credit and authority with us, the Apostle testifies, saying of it, We have also a more sure word of prophecy, whereunto you do well that you take heed, as unto a light that shines in a dark place, until the day dawns, and the Morning Star arises in your hearts (2 Peter 1:19).

Furthermore, all the Evangelists confirm unto us that these things were done exactly according to those Scriptures.[113] The Apostle also states:

Christ died for us, according to the Scriptures; and that he was buried, and that he arose again on the Third Day, according to the Scriptures. And that he was seen of Cephas, and then of the Twelve. After that he was seen of above five hundred brethren at once, of whom the greater part remain unto this present, but some have fallen asleep. After that he was seen of James, then of all the Apostles. And last of all, he was seen of me also, as of one born out of due time. (1 Corinthians 15:3-8)

The Prophet Jonah had also, of old, beautifully represented (τύπος) the Resurrection of Christ; as our Lord Jesus Christ applied it to himself when he spoke to the Jews, saying:

An evil and adulterous generation seeks after a sign, and there shall no sign be given unto it but the Sign of the Prophet Jonah. For as Jonah was three days and three nights in the belly of the whale, so shall the Son of Man be three days and three nights in the heart of the earth. (Matthew 12:39-40; cf. Jonah 1:17; 2:1-10)

c32C

The Sixth Article: Of the Ascension.

55. What is the Sixth Article of the Faith?

Who ascended into heaven, and sits at the right hand of the Father.

56. What are we taught by this Article?

Four Doctrines.

First, That Christ ascended into heaven, and sat down, with glory and honor, at the right hand of God; with that very same body in which he had truly and really suffered the torments of the Cross, and with which he had arisen from the dead.

Secondly, That he ascended into heaven only as man, for as God he was always there, and in all places.

Thirdly, That Christ never after put off the human nature which he had taken upon him of the blessed Virgin, and that he will hereafter come again to Judgment therewith; as the Angels spoke to the Apostles, This same Jesus which is taken up from you into heaven shall so come in like manner as you have seen him go into heaven (Acts 1:11).

Fourthly, We are hereby taught the body of Christ is in heaven only, and not on the earth after the manner it used to be according to the flesh he wore;[114] but only after a sacramental mode (μυστηριώδη τρόπον); whereby, in the Eucharist, the same Son of God, God and man, is present on earth by a change of substance (Greek: μετουσίωσις; Latin: transsubstantiatio), for the substance (ουσία) of the bread is changed into the substance (μεταβάλλεται εἱς τὴν οὐσίαν) of his most holy Body, and the substance (ουσία) of the wine into the substance (ουσία) of his most precious Blood. Wherefore we ought to glorify and reverence the holy Eucharist as our Savior Jesus himself.

c32V

The Seventh Article: Of the Second Coming.

57. What is the Seventh Article of the Faith?

He shall come again with glory to judge both the living and the dead, whose Kingdom shall have no End.

58. What does this Article teach us?

Three things.

First, That Christ will come again, to judge the living and the dead; as he himself says, When the Son of Man shall come in his glory, and all the holy Angels with him (Matthew 25:31). And this coming will be with swiftness, As the lightning comes out of the east, and shines even unto the west, so also shall the coming of the Son of Man be (Matthew 24:27); Also, But of that day and hour no man knows; no, not the Angels (24:36). But first it must be that these things happen, namely, That the Gospel be preached unto all nations (24:14); that Antichrist come (24:24); that there be horrid and inhuman wars, famine, and pestilence (24:7); and the like. In a word, that there be many and great afflictions, according to the word of the Lord, Then shall he great tribulation, such as was not since the beginning of the world to this time, no, nor ever shall he after (24:21).

Of this Judgment the Apostle thus plainly teaches, I charge you, therefore, before God, and the Lord Jesus Christ, who shall judge the living and the dead, at his appearing and his Kingdom (2 Timothy 4:1).

59. What is the second doctrine contained in this Article?

The second is that in this Last Judgment all men are to give an account of all their thoughts, words, and works, as the Scripture testifies, I say unto you, that every idle word that men shall speak, they shall give an account thereof in the Day of Judgment (Matthew 12:36). And so the Apostle:

Therefore judge nothing before the Time, until the Lord comes, who both will bring to light the hidden things of darkness, and will make manifest the counsels of the heart; and then shall every man have his praise of God. (1 Corinthians 4:5)

60. What is the third thing taught in this Article?

The third is how in that day every one shall receive a full and everlasting reward, according to his merit; some receiving this sentence, Come, you who are blessed of my Father, inherit the Kingdom prepared for you from the beginning of the world (Matthew 25:34). And to others shall be pronounced this afflicting sound, Depart from me, you cursed, into everlasting fire, prepared for the Devil and his Angels (Matthew 25:41); Where their worm dies not, and the fire is not quenched (Mark 9:44).

61. Although in that Day all men in general must give an account of their actions and affairs; I would like to know whether everyone, at his departure from this life, gives an account of his life, and answers, as it were, in a Particular Judgment (κριτήριον μερικὸν).

The Day of the Last Judgment (τελευταίας κρίσεως) will not be by inquiring after every minute circumstance, for all things are known and manifest unto God; and as everyone, at the time of his death, is fully conscious to himself of all his sins, so does every one, after death, very well know what is to be the payment for his works;

For as his works are clearly manifest, so is the will of God concerning them also clearly manifest. As St. Gregory of Nazianzus, the Theologian, says in the Funeral Oration (Oration 7) for his brother, St. Caesarius:

I am induced to believe, that, as wise men say, the good and acceptable soul, when its espousal with the body is dissolved, enjoying with the powers of its mind the good which it possesses (for that which before clouded it with darkness being now purged away, or laid aside, or what no words can express), is enraptured, and exults with a most singular and transporting joy, and flies rejoicing to its Lord (while it escapes from this life, as from a loathsome prison, and spurns under its feet the shackles which fettered before the wings of its mind) to taste, as in imagination, the bliss in store for it.

And when, not long after, it again receives its well-known body from the earth, which first supplied, and now had kept it safe in store; after a manner only known to God, who first joined, and afterwards separated them; with that body, wherein it had before lived the heavenly life, it enters now united, with the heavenly glory as their inheritance.

The wicked souls may be considered in the same manner; namely, that they are immediately aware of the torments that await them, howbeit, neither the just nor the wicked receive the full recompense of their works before the Last Judgment; nor are they all in one state, nor limited to one place.

Now, from hence it is clear enough that this could not be before the Last Judgment (τελευταίας κρίσεως) without some kind of Particular Judgment (κρίσεως μερικῆς): And therefore there is such a Particular Judgment (μερικὸν κριτήριον) as this. When, therefore, we say that God does not require an exact account of our lives, it is to be understood that we mean, not according to the forms and weakness of human tribunals.

62. Are not all the souls of the saints placed in the same degree of happiness after death?

As the souls do not all go out of this life in the same degree of divine grace, so neither after their departure are they in one and the same degree of happiness. This we learn from Christ himself, In my Father's house are many mansions (John 14:2). And elsewhere, Her sins, which are many, are forgiven; for she loved much: But to whom little is forgiven, the same loves little (Luke 7:47). To the same purpose speaks the Apostle, Who will render unto every man according to his works (Romans 2:6).

63. What are we to think concerning those who depart hence under the wrath of God?

Of these, after the Final Judgment (ἐσχἀτην κρίσιν), some will receive greater torments (μεγαλητέρην κόλασιν), some lesser; but both will be without end (Greek: αἰωνίως; Latin: aeternis omnes tormentis cruciatum iri), As the Scripture declares:

That servant that knew his Lord's will, and prepared not himself, neither did according to his will, shall be beaten with many lashes: But he that knew not, and did commit things worthy of stripes, shall be beaten with few lashes. (Luke 12:47-48)

64. Do not some die, so as to be in a medium between the blessed and the damned?

Of these there are not any; nevertheless, it is certain that many sinners are freed from the bonds of Hades; not by their own repentance or confession, as the Scripture says, In Hades who shall give you thanks? (Psalm 6:5) And elsewhere, The dead shall not praise you, O Lord; nor any that go down into Hades (Psalm 113:17 LXX); but with the blessings of the living (μὲ τὰς εὐποιΐας τῶν ζώντων),[115] and for the prayers of the Church, made in their behalf; and especially for the sake of the Bloodless Sacrifice (τὴν ἀναίμακτον θυσίαν, i.e. as at the Divine Liturgy) which the Church daily offers up for the living and the dead; in like manner as Christ also died for both.

But the souls of such are by no means to be delivered by their own works; as Blessed Theophylact, commenting on these words of Christ, To whom power is given of forgiving sins on earth (Luke 5:24), teaches; saying:

Observe that sins are forgiven on earth; for so long as we continue on earth we can wipe out our sins by repentance, but after we leave this earth we are no more able of ourselves to cancel our sins by our confessions. The doors then are shut.

And again, on the words of Matthew, Bind him hand and foot (Matthew 22:13), by which the active faculties of the soul are meant, he says:

In this life we may labor and endeavour, but afterwards the active faculties of the soul are bound, nor can we do anymore to outweigh our offences.

And further, commenting on Matthew 25:6-13, he says, There is no more time for repentance and good works after this life.

From all which it is clear, that after its separation the soul can no more repent (μετανοέω), nor do any other work whereby it might be freed from the bondage of Hades. Therefore, only the Divine Liturgy, the prayers and charitable deeds, which are performed by the living, for their sakes, do comfort and greatly benefit the souls, and free them from the bondage of Hades.

65. What, then, are we to think concerning charitable giving and good works, which are performed for the comfort of the departed?

Blessed Theophylact, expounding these words of Christ, Fear him who has power (ἐξουσία) to cast into Hell (γέεννα; Gehenna) (Luke 12:5), thus treats of this matter:

Observe, my brethren, Christ says not, “Fear him who, after he has killed, casts into Hell (γέεννα),” but who has power(ἐξουσία) to cast into Hell. For he does not cast all who died in their sins into Hell, but it is in the hand of God to do so, and also to forgive them. This, I say, concerning the pious offerings and intercessions which are made for the good of those that sleep. For these things are of no small benefit, even to those who depart hence in the most grievous state of sin. God does not, then, cast the guilty into Hell when he has killed them; but he has power to cast them into Hell. Wherefore let us not cease to endeavour, again and again, by our charitable giving and our intercessions, to implore his mercy, who, having the power to cast into Hell, does not always exert that power; but also has the ability (δύναμαι) to forgive.

We are therefore taught by the holy Scripture, and the commentary of this Father, that we ought, by all means, to pray for the departed, to offer the Bloodless Sacrifice (θυσίας ἀναιμάκτους) for them, and to dispense our charitable giving with a liberal hand; seeing they can no more perform these good works for themselves.

66. What are we to think of the fire of purgatory (τὸ πῦρ τὸ καθαρτήριον)?

It is nowhere taught in the holy Scriptures that there is any temporary punishment, whereby the soul, after death, may be purged. On the contrary, the Church, in the Second Council of Constantinople (i.e. the Fifth Ecumenical Council held in 553), did condemn Origen for this very opinion (γνώμη).[116]

Moreover, it is evident that the soul, when once departed, cannot again become a partaker of the sacraments of the Church. If this could be, that the soul satisfy there for sins committed in this life, then, by like reason, it might partake of the sacraments of penance there; which being contrary to orthodox doctrine, the Church rightly and wisely offers the Unbloody Sacrifice (ἀναίμακτον θυσίαν) for those souls, together with her prayers, that they may be forgiven those things wherein they had offended while they continued in this life: And not that they might be delivered from any punishment (κόλασις) that they were then suffering for a time only.

Our Church does not admit or approve of such fables as some men have fancied concerning the state of souls after death; as that they are tormented in pits and waters, and with skewers, when they are snatched away by death (before they can have done sufficient penance for their faults).

67. What place is particularly appointed for those souls that go hence in a state of grace and favor with God?

Those souls of men which depart hence in the grace of God (τήν χάριν τοῦ Θεοῦ), and have wiped out their sins by repentance (μετάνοια), have their place in the hand of God.

As says the holy Scripture, The souls of the righteous are in the hand of God, and there shall no torments touch them (Wisdom 3:1). Their place is also named Paradise, as our Lord Christ called it to the thief on the Cross, Assuredly I say to you, This day you shall be with me in Paradise (Luke 23:43).

It is also called Abraham's Bosom; as in Luke, And it came to pass that the beggar died, and was carried by the Angels into Abraham's Bosom (Luke 16:22).

Sometimes it is named the Kingdom of Heaven, as it was by our Lord:

I say unto you, that many shall come from the East and West, and shall sit down with Abraham, and Isaac, and Jacob in the Kingdom of Heaven. (Matthew 8:11)

By whichsoever of these three names that we have mentioned any one shall call the place of righteous souls, he will not err; provided that he believes and understands this much, that they enjoy the grace of God (τήν χάριν τοῦ Θεοῦ), and are in his heavenly Kingdom, and, as the Hymns of the Church mention, in Heaven.

68. Where is the place of those souls who leave their bodies under divine wrath (θεϊκὴν ὀργὴν)?

Many names are given to that place: It is called Hades (ᾅδης), into which the Devil, when cast out of Heaven, was driven; as the Prophet testifies:

I will ascend above the heights of the clouds; I will be like the Most High, says Satan. Yet you shall be brought down to Hades, to the lowest depths of the pit. (Isaiah 14:14-15)

Again, it is called everlasting fire(πῦρ αἰώνιον); as the Scripture says, Depart from me, you cursed, into everlasting fire, prepared for the Devil and his Angels (Matthew 25:41).

Likewise it is named outer darkness(σκότος ἐξώτερον), Cast the unprofitable servant into outer darkness; there shall be wailing and gnashing of teeth (Matthew 25:30).

It is called by many other names, all of which mean a place of condemnation (τὀπος τῆς κατακρίσεως) and the divine wrath (τῆς θείας ὀργῆς).

To this place go down the souls of all those who die at enmity with God, and under his wrath; and here are they damned.

This, then, is to be believed by the faithful, that as the souls of the righteous, although received into Heaven, do not receive the full and perfect crown of glory before the Last Judgment, so neither do the souls of the damned feel and suffer the full measure and weight of the punishments before that time.

But after that final and decisive Judgment, the souls of all, rejoined to their bodies, will be crowned with glory or overwhelmed with torments.

c34V

The Eighth Article: Of the Holy Spirit.

69. What is the Eighth Article of the Faith?

And in the Holy Spirit, the Lord, the Giver of Life, who proceeds from the Father, who with the Father and the Son together is worshipped and glorified, who spoke by the Prophets.

70. What does this Article teach?

Three things.

First, That the Holy Spirit is God, of the same substance (Greek: ὁμοούσιος; Latin: consubstantialem) with the Father and the Son; as these words of the Apostle clearly show:

There are diversities of gifts, but the same Spirit: And differences of ministries, but the same Lord: And there are diversities of operations, but it is the same God that works all in all. (1 Corinthians 12:4-6)

And again, The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ, and the love of God, and the communion of the Holy Spirit, be with you all (2 Corinthians 13:14).

Now, whereas, in these texts the Holy Spirit is sometimes named first, and sometimes the Son, it is because all the three Persons are of one essence (ὁμοούσια) and partakers of equal honors (ἰσὀτιμα). The Son and the Holy Spirit are, both of them immediately (ἀμέσως) and equally (ὁμοίως), of one essence (μίαν οὐσίαν) and glory (Latin: gloriae) with the Father; the Father being the Origin (originem) of the Son and the Spirit: the Son as being Begotten (generationem) and the Holy Spirit as Proceeding (processionem).[117]

According to what Peter declares to Ananias in the Acts of the Apostles, Why has Satan filled your heart to lie to the Holy Spirit? (Acts 5:3) And presently, after he concludes, says, You have not lied unto men, but to God (Acts 5:4). The Holy Spirit is, therefore, certainly true and very God.

71. What is the second thing taught in this Article?

That the Holy Spirit proceeds (ἐκπορεύομαι; Latin: procedit) from the Father alone (μόνου; Latin: solo), as the Source (fonte) and Principle (origine) of his Divinity (Greek: ὡς πηγῆς καὶ ἀρχῆς τῆς θεότητος); as our Savior himself teaches us:

When the Comforter comes, whom I will send to you from the Father; the Spirit of Truth, who proceeds (ἐκπορεύομαι) from the Father. (John 15:26)

St. Athanasius lays down the same doctrine in his Creed (line 23), The Holy Spirit is of the Father, not made, nor created, nor begotten, but proceeding.[118] And elsewhere in his works:

God and Father, he only is the cause of the other two, and unbegotten. The Son, begotten, and sprung from the Father only, the cause of his origin. The Holy Spirit himself also springs and proceeds only from the Father, as his cause, and by the Son was sent into the world. (Holy Questions, vol. 2.43)[119]

And St. Gregory the Theologian says:

The Holy Spirit, who Proceeds from the Father, is Uncreated, as being Proceeding; as being Unbegotten, he is not the Son; but as being between Unbegotten and Begotten, he is God. (Oration 31: Fifth Theological Oration, paragraph 8)

Since we have already treated of this matter at large in the First Article, let it, therefore, suffice us that we hold what Christ himself taught; what the catholic and orthodox Eastern Church believes and altogether professed in the Second Ecumenical Council; and let us hold fast the Faith, without adding: “And from the Son,” as the Church has commanded.[120]

Nay, not only the orthodox and catholic Eastern Church has passed a heavy censure on those who add these words, but also the Western Roman Church. This is evident from the two Silver Tables, on one of which the Creed was engraved in Greek, and on the other in Latin, without this addition: “And from the Son”; which Tables were, by order of Leo the Third, Pope of Rome, affixed up in St. Peters Church, in the Year of our Lord 809, as Baronius confessed.

Whosoever, therefore, continues firm and constant in this the Faith, he may have undoubting hope of his salvation, as one who does not turn aside from the common opinion (τὴν κοινήν γνώμην) of the Church.

72. What is the third thing taught in this Article?

That the Holy Spirit is the real author of the holy Scripture, both of the Old and of the New Testaments; and wrote them by the hands of many co-workers (πολλῶν συνεργῶν): Wherefore the Scriptures of the Old Testament, and also of the New, is the teaching of the Holy Spirit.

And whatsoever the holy Fathers have decreed in Ecumenical and Particular Orthodox Councils, wheresoever they were held, is taught of the Holy Spirit. The holy Apostles speak thus in their council, It seemed good to the Holy Spirit, and to us (Acts 15:28): After whose example other Orthodox Councils have, in the same style, concluded their decrees.[121]

On the Gifts of the Holy Spirit.

73. What, and how many, are the Gifts of the Holy Spirit?

Seven:

Wisdom 

Understanding 

Counsel 

Strength 

Knowledge 

Godliness 

Fear of God 

Of these Gifts the holy Scripture speaks thus, And there were seven Lamps of Fire burning before the Throne, which are the seven Spirits of God (Revelation 4:5). Now, these Gifts of the Spirit, or, to speak more properly, the Holy Spirit himself, was in Christ after a more abundant and perfect manner than ever in any other man, as says the Prophet Isaiah:

And the Spirit of the Lord shall rest upon him, the Spirit of Wisdom and Understanding, the Spirit of Counsel and Might, the Spirit of Knowledge, and of the Fear of the Lord. (Isaiah 11:2)

This the Evangelist St. John confirms with his testimony:

And the Word was made flesh, and dwelt among us; and we beheld his glory, the glory as of the only begotten of the Father, full of grace and truth. (John 1:14)

And, Of his fullness we have all received, and grace upon grace (John 1:16). For the Holy Spirit was in Christ, as being consubstantial (ὁμοούσιος) with him according to his divinity (κατά τὴν θεότητα); and filled him with grace and wisdom, as it is written, And the child grew, and waxed strong in Spirit, filled with wisdom, and the grace of God was upon him (Luke 2:40). This is to be understood of the human nature of Christ.

74. What is the first Gift of the Holy Spirit?

The first Gift is wisdom (σοφία; Latin: sapientia); namely, that wisdom which is from above, of which the Apostle thus speaks:

The wisdom that is from above is first pure, then peaceable, gentle, and easy to be entreated, full of mercy and good fruits, without partiality, and without hypocrisy. (James 3:17)

And this is the contrary of carnal wisdom, according to the Apostle, In simplicity and godly sincerity, not with fleshly wisdom, but by the grace of God, we have conducted ourselves in the world (2 Corinthians 1:12). Which fleshly and worldly wisdom the same Apostle further speaks of, rehearsing the Old Testament:

For it is written, “I will destroy the wisdom of the wise, and will bring to nothing the understanding of the intelligent” (Isaiah 29:14). Where is the wise? Where is the scribe? Where is the disputer of this age? Has God not made foolish the wisdom of this world? (1 Corinthians 1:19-20; cf. Isaiah 33:18)

75. What is the second Gift of the Holy Spirit?

The Gift of understanding (συνέσεως; Latin: intelligentiae), or the knowledge of the hidden and secret things of the divine will, whereof the Scripture thus teaches:

Everyone wise in understanding in whom the Lord put wisdom and understanding, to know how to work all manner of work for the service of the sanctuary, according to all that the Lord had commanded. (Exodus 36:1)

And of Daniel and his companions, God gave them knowledge and skill in all learning and Wisdom, and Daniel had Understanding in all Visions and Dreams (Daniel 1:17). And also, Then he opened their understanding, that they might understand the Scriptures (Luke 24:45). And the Apostle, May the Lord give you understanding in all things (2 Timothy 2:7).

Contrary to this is folly and disbelief; of which our Lord says thus, Fool, and slow of heart to believe all that the Prophets have spoken (Luke 24:25). And elsewhere the Apostle, Are you so foolish? Having begun in the Spirit, are you now made perfect by the flesh? (Galatians 3:3)

76. What is the third Gift of the Holy Spirit?

The third Gift of the Holy Spirit is counsel (βουλὴ; Latin: consilium), which serves to carry to the divine glory and the salvation of men's souls, and is nearly the same as justice.

Of this counsel the Scripture speaks, For I did not shrink from declaring unto you the whole counsel of God (Acts 20:27).

Opposite to this is the counsel of the ungodly; of which the divine Psalmist sings, Blessed is the man who has not walked in the counsel of the ungodly (Psalm 1:1). And again:

The Lord brings the counsel of the nations to nothing, and makes the calculations of the people to be of no effect, and casts out the counsels of princes. (Psalm 32:10 LXX)

77. What is the fourth Gift of the Holy Spirit?

Strength (ἰσχὺς; Latin: robur). For, maintaining all constancy and fortitude in the Faith, we ought bravely to resist all temptations: Of which strength of mind the Scriptures speak thus, Watch, stand fast in the Faith, act like men, be strong (1 Corinthians 16:13). And:

Stand, therefore, having your waist fastened about with truth, and having on the breastplate of righteousness; and your feet shod with the preparation of the gospel of peace; above all, taking the shield of faith, wherewith you shall be able to quench all the fiery darts of the wicked; and take the helmet of salvation, and the sword of the Spirit, which is the Word of God. (Ephesians 6:14-17)

Contrary to this strength is fear; of which the Holy Prophet David says, They were brought in great fear, even where no fear was (Psalm 13:5 LXX; cf. Psalm 53:5). And our Lord Jesus Christ forbids to have this fear, Fear not those that kill the body, and after that have no more that they can do (Luke 12:4).

78. What is the fifth Gift of the Holy Spirit?

Knowledge (γνῶσις; Latin: cognitio), which the holy Psalmist thus describes, Who instructs the nations, shall not he chasten? It is he that teaches man knowledge (Psalm 94:10). And the Prophet Jeremiah, I will give you shepherds according to my heart, who shall feed you with knowledge and understanding (Jeremiah 3:15).

Which knowledge and understanding is chiefly to be understood and explained to mean the knowledge of the will and law of God.

Contrary to this is ignorance; namely, of the divine will and law: as says the Psalmist:

Pour out your indignation upon the nations that have not known you, and upon the kingdoms that have not called upon your Name. (Psalm 79:6)

79. What is the sixth Gift of the Holy Spirit?

Godliness (ευσέβεια; Latin: pietas), which with right faith is founded on constant, fervent prayer and good works; of which the Apostle says, Godliness is profitable unto all things, having promise of the life that now is, and of that which is to come (1 Timothy 4:8).

Therefore are those truly called godly who continually worship God with prayer, and shun everything that pertains to sin. Godliness, I say, not showy and specious, as was that formerly of the Pharisees, but solid and genuine, deep rooted in the bottom of the heart, and to which this saying of our Lord's cannot be applied, This people honors me with their lips, but their heart is far from me (Matthew 15:8; cf. Isaiah 29:13). And again, You blind Pharisee, cleanse first that which is within the cup and dish, that the outside of them may be clean also (Matthew 23:26).

80. What is the Seventh Gift of the Holy Spirit?

The Fear of God (ὁ φόβος τοῦ Θεοῦ; Latin: timor Dei), which ought to be like the fear of children towards their parents, and not like the fear of servants towards their masters.

Of this proper, right fear the holy Psalmist sings, O fear the Lord, you his saints, for they that fear him lack nothing (Psalm 34:9).

But of the other sort of Fear the Apostle says thus, There is no fear in love, but perfect love casts out fear; because fear has torment; he that fears is not made perfect in love (1 John 4:18).

And the Scripture teaches us that we should fear God for love, O praise the Lord, you that fear him. Glorify him, all you of the seed of Jacob; and fear him, all you seed of Israel (Psalm 22:23).

He that thus fears the Lord will keep his Commandments, as it is said, If a man loves me, he will keep my word (John 14:23; cf. John 14:21).

81. What, and how many, are the Fruits of the Holy Spirit?

Saint Paul lists nine Fruits of the Holy Spirit (καρποὺς τοῦ ἁγίου Πνεύματος), or Signs of divine grace (σημάσια τῆς θείας χάριτος), The Fruit of the Spirit is love, joy, peace, patience, kindness, goodness, faithfulness, gentleness, self-control (Galatians 5:22-23a).[122]

But we are, moreover, to call and account all other virtues Fruits of the Holy Spirit, because they come down from him, and by his grace are rightly practised by men: And, therefore, St. Paul does not add, against these there is no law (Galatians 5:23b), as if there were a law against any other such kind of virtue: there being many like unto these.

c37N

The Ninth Article: Of the Church.

82. What is the Ninth Article of the Faith?

In one, holy, catholic, and apostolic Church.

83. What does the holy Church teach in this Article of the Faith?

Four things. First, That the Church is one, holy, catholic and apostolic; according to the doctrine of the Apostle, I have espoused you to one Husband, that I may present you as a pure Virgin unto Christ (2 Corinthians 11:2). For like as Christ is only one, so his Bride also can be but one; as is manifest from the Epistle to the Ephesians, One Lord, one Faith, one Baptism, one God and Father of all (Ephesians 4:5-6).

84. What is the second thing contained in this Article?

The second thing taught in this Article is, that the Church does not take this name of catholic Church from anyone place (τόπον) or see predominant over all others; For those are particular churches which are in particular places; As, for example, the Church in Ephesus, in Philadelphia, in Laodicea, in Antioch, in Jerusalem, in Rome, in Alexandria, and others.

However, among these particular churches she may well be called the mother (μήτηρ) who was honored first with the presence of Christ, and received eternal life and remission of sins, and from which the Gospel was first preached and spread through the whole world; As the Scripture bears witness:

Thus it was necessary for Christ to suffer, and to rise from the dead the third day. And that repentance and remission of sins should be preached in his Name among all nations, beginning at Jerusalem, and you are witnesses of these things. (Luke 24:46-48)

And elsewhere, You shall be witnesses unto me both in Jerusalem, and in all Judea, and in Samaria, and unto the uttermost parts of the earth (Acts 1:8). Yet she is called first (πρῶτος) who outshone all other churches in sanctity of doctrine (διδασκαλία) and moral character (ἦθος), and to whose judgment the Apostles submitted their actions; as the Scripture tells us:

And when Peter was come up to Jerusalem, they that were of the Circumcision contended with him, saying, “You went to men uncircumcised, and did eat with them.” (Acts 11:2-3)

To which Peter answered:

What was I, that I could withstand God? When they heard these things they held their peace, and glorified God, saying, “Then God has also granted to the Gentiles repentance unto life.” (Acts 11:17-18)

And:

Then tidings of these things came unto the ears of the Church in Jerusalem; and they sent forth Barnabas, that he should go as far as Antioch. (Acts 11:22)

And elsewhere:

They determined that Paul and Barnabas, and certain others of them, should go up to Jerusalem unto the Apostles and Elders about this question. (Acts 15:2)

And:

Then it pleased the Apostles and Elders, with the whole Church, to send chosen men of their own company to Antioch with Paul and Barnabas... and wrote Letters by them after this manner... It seemed good unto the Holy Spirit, and to us, to lay no greater burden upon you than those necessary things. (Acts 15:22-23, 28)

Further also of the same:

And as they went through the cities, they delivered to them for observance (φυλάσσω) the decrees (δόγμα) which were ordained (κρίνω) by the Apostles and Elders which were at Jerusalem. (Acts 16:4)

The Church of Jerusalem, therefore, is without doubt the mother (μήτηρ) of all other churches, and first (πρώτη; Latin: princeps): forasmuch as the Gospel was spread from her over the whole world (although, indeed, in later times, the Emperors gave the precedence to Old and New Rome, for the honor of the Empire, which they became the Seats of, according to the third Canon of the Second Ecumenical Council, at Constantinople).[123]

Nevertheless, this Church of Jerusalem was the universal (καθολική) Church, as all nations received their faith and doctrine from her.

85. What is the third thing contained in this Article?

That Jesus Christ is the only foundation of the Church, according to the words of the Apostle, No other foundation can anyone lay than that which is laid, which is Jesus Christ (1 Corinthians 3:11).

Although on some occasions the Apostles and Prophets are called the foundations of the Faith and of the Church; as when St. John says:

That the great city, Jerusalem, was enclosed with a wall, having twelve foundations, and in them the names of the Twelve Apostles of the Lamb were written. (Revelation 21:14)

And St. Paul affirms that we are built upon the foundations of the Apostles and Prophets (Ephesians 2:20).

This is to be understood, not as if the Apostles and Prophets were these foundations of themselves and in the first instance; for in that sense Christ only is the foundation; but secondarily, and with relation to Him, as being themselves laid next upon the foundation of the doctrine of salvation of our Lord Jesus Christ, as being the first who propagated the Faith of Christ over the whole world. For Christ has not founded his Church on any mortal men, but only upon himself, and on his own divine doctrine.

Moreover, we are taught, in this Article, that Christ is the only Head of his Church; according as we are taught by the Apostle, For the husband is the head of the wife, and Christ is the Head of the Church; and he is the Savior of the Body (Ephesians 5:23). And again:

He is the Head of the Body, the Church, who is the beginning, the first-born from the dead; that in all things he might have the preeminence. (Colossians 1:18)

However, the rulers (προΐστημι) of the Church are called heads (κεφαλή), in their several churches over which they are chief priests (ἀρχιερεῖς); but this is only as stewards and deputies (vicarius) of Christ, in his several provinces, over which they are said to be heads. Thus the holy Scripture speaks then:

Take heed, therefore, unto yourselves, and unto the whole flock, over which the Holy Spirit has made you Bishops (ἐπίσκοπος, literally overseers), to feed the Churches of God, which he has purchased with his own blood. (Acts 20:28)

In suchwise, however, that Christ himself is the Head and Chief of the Shepherds; as St. Peter testifies, When the chief Shepherd appears, you shall receive the unfading crown of glory (1 Peter 5:4).

86. What is the fourth thing taught in this Article?
